## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (mathematical biology) — single-species population dynamics
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time derivative of population size P, indicating an underlying ordinary differential equation for single-population growth. Common mechanisms include per-capita reproduction, density dependence (crowding/carrying capacity), Allee effects, harvesting, immigration, and environmental/seasonal forcing via explicit time dependence t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian growth (exponential ODE): dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Net immigration/emigration + growth: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (constant influx/outflux plus proportional growth/decline)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (positive or negative quadratic density effects depending on sign)
- Self-limitation (quadratic crowding): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (crowding reduces growth at high P)
- Richards / generalized logistic family: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P**c2) (flexible approach to carrying capacity with shape parameter)
- Theta-logistic form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (nonlinear density dependence in the crowding term)
- Gompertz-type regulation: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / (P + c2)) (per-capita growth declines roughly logarithmically with P)
- Ricker-type continuous inhibition: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (strong crowding suppression via exponential factor)
- Strong Allee effect (cubic with three equilibria): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (extinction threshold at P=c1 and carrying-capacity-like root at P=1/c2)
- Weak Allee effect (reduced growth at low P): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * P**2 (low-density boost without a strict threshold depending on parameters)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 (fixed removal rate; can induce extinction if too large)
- Proportional harvesting/extra mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P (additional per-capita loss such as fishing or predation proxy)
- Seasonal forcing of per-capita growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting reproduction/survival)
- Seasonal forcing plus baseline immigration: dP_dt = c0 + (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4)) * P (both additive and multiplicative seasonal drivers)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth diagnosis: the structure (dP_dt / P) being approximately constant suggests density-independent growth; a decreasing function of P indicates negative density dependence.
- Equilibria encoded by factors: expressions like P*(1 - c*P) or P*(P-cA)*(1-cK*P) directly imply equilibrium points (zeros of dP_dt) and allow interpretation as extinction, Allee threshold, and carrying capacity.
- Allee effect signature: an additional positive root (P - c1) in dP_dt beyond P=0 indicates a critical minimum population below which dP_dt < 0 (possible extinction threshold).
- Crowding mechanism choice: a negative quadratic term (-c*P**2) implies pairwise competition; an exp(-c*P) factor implies rapidly increasing inhibition at high density (strong crowding).
- Harvesting/management signal: an additive negative constant term (-c) represents constant-yield removal and can eliminate positive equilibria; a negative linear term (-c*P) represents proportional mortality shifting the effective growth rate.
- Seasonality/environmental variability: sinusoidal dependence on t in coefficients indicates periodic forcing; this can create recurrent booms/busts even if the autonomous (time-invariant) system has a stable equilibrium.
- Stability intuition from slope: near an equilibrium P*, if d/dP(dP_dt) at P* is negative, the equilibrium is locally stable; positive indicates instability (useful when interpreting fitted symbolic forms).
- Regime separation by low vs high P: terms like +c*P (growth) and -c*P**2 (competition) imply low-density growth dominated by linear terms and high-density decline dominated by higher powers.

GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P/t**c6
Candidate formulas: 69

GT:
\[
0.1404201691\;(-1+P/4.5321236761)\,(1-P/78.4907131146)\,P \;+\; 0.1404201691\; \frac{P}{t^{4.5321236761}}
\]
Structure facts:
- It is the sum of (i) a **cubic polynomial in \(P\)** (expand: \(k(P^3\cdot\text{const}+P^2\cdot\text{const}+P\cdot\text{const})\)) and (ii) a **separable term** \(k\,P\,t^{-a}\) with a **negative power of \(t\)** and **no other \(t\)-dependence**.
- No denominators in \(P\), no trig/log/exp, no \(|P|\).

So any matching candidate must be able to represent:
1) a general cubic polynomial in \(P\) (with specific coefficients), plus  
2) exactly \( \text{const}\cdot P\cdot t^{\text{(negative exponent)}}\).

Now check candidates:

1. Has \(P c2 t^{c3}\) (positive/any power but not forced negative) plus rational \(P*c4/(P+c5)\) and sine. To match GT, must kill rational and sine (set c4=0, c6=0). Left with \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P c2 t^{c3}\): cannot produce a \(P^3\) term. No match.

2. Has exp(P*c1)/(P*c2+c3) rational-in-P and also \(t^{c6}\) in numerator over same denominator. To remove denominator dependence you’d need \(c2=0\) and then still have exp(P*c1) unless c1=0; then expression becomes polynomial in P but the \(t\)-term becomes \(P*c5*t^{c6}/c3\) (power of t, not \(t^{-a}\) unless choose negative exponent—possible), but still overall only up to \(P^2\) (since first term is \(P^2*c0/(c3)\), no \(P^3\)). No match.

3. \(P^2 c0 + P*P^{c1}c2\) can make \(P^3\) by setting \(c1=2\). But the \(t\)-dependence is \(P*c4*(c5+t)^{c6}\), which is a shifted power \((t+c5)^{c6}\), not \(t^{-a}\) for all t unless \(c5=0\). If set \(c5=0\), it becomes \(P*c4*t^{c6}\) and we can set \(c6=-4.532...\). Then the remaining P-polynomial terms: \(P^2 c0 + P^{3}c2 + P*c3 + P*c7\) can match cubic+quadratic+linear (combine linear via c3+c7). This one *could* match the overall form. But note GT cubic part is **not just any cubic**: it is \(kP(-1+P/A)(1-P/B)\) which indeed is a cubic with no constant term—candidate can represent any cubic with no constant term. So candidate 3 is potentially matchable. (Keep for final consistency check.)

4. Has \(P*c2*(P*c3)^{c4} = P^{c4+1}\cdot(\text{const})\). Can make \(P^3\) by \(c4=2\). Also has \(P*c5*(c6+t)^{c7}\) which can become \(P*t^{-a}\) only if \(c6=0\) and \(c7=-4.532...\). Then remaining polynomial terms \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P^3(\cdot) + P c8\) can match cubic/quadratic/linear. So candidate 4 is also potentially matchable.

5. Polynomial part is \(P^3 c0 + P^2(c1+c2+c3)+P(c4+c5)+ P*c6*(c7+t)^{c8}\). The \(t\)-term can be \(P*t^{-a}\) if \(c7=0\), \(c8=-4.532...\). Then polynomial can match cubic/quadratic/linear. Potentially matchable.

6. Contains \(P*c0*exp(P*c1)\) and \(P^{c5}c6\). To get a pure polynomial, need \(c1=0\) so exp=1, giving linear term only; and \(P^{c5}\) could give \(P^2\) or \(P^3\) but then it’s not multiplied by P necessarily. Still cannot generally produce both \(P^3\) and \(P^2\) and \(P\) with correct degrees simultaneously while also having \(P*c2*t^{c3}\) as \(P*t^{-a}\) (possible). But the exp term becomes just linear, leaving only one power term \(P^{c5}\). You can’t get both \(P^2\) and \(P^3\) unless \(c5\) somehow yields both (impossible). No match.

7. Rational /(P+c2) form; cannot equal a polynomial in P for all P unless numerator cancels denominator exactly, but numerator is sum of terms with different P-dependence including exp(P*c1) and \(P^{c3}\). Not possible to become exact cubic polynomial + separable \(P t^{-a}\). No match.

8. Like (1) but last term \(P^{c6}c7\) (power). Kill rational by c4=0. Then can make \(P^3\) via \(c6=3\). Still only one additional power term besides \(P^2\) and \(P\), so polynomial part can be cubic+quadratic+linear (yes). And \(P*c2*t^{c3}\) can be \(P*t^{-a}\) by choosing negative exponent. So candidate 8 is potentially matchable.

9. Has sine term; set its coefficient c7=0. Remaining \(P^2 c0 + P*P^{c1}c2\) can make \(P^3\) with \(c1=2\). \(P*c4*t^{c5}\) can be \(P*t^{-a}\) with \(c5=-4.532...\). Linear terms combine. Potentially matchable.

10. Has sine and also \(exp(c8*Abs(P))*cos(c9*t)\). To match GT must remove both: set c4=0 and c7=0. Then left \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P c2 t^{c3}\): no \(P^3\). No match.

11. Has logs in P; cannot become polynomial in P for all P unless log coefficients are 0. Setting those to 0 leaves only linear in P and \(P t^{c2}\), no \(P^3\). No match.

12. \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P c2 t^{c3} + P^{c4} c5 t^{c6}\). Hard to get cubic polynomial in P without extra t dependence: if set \(c6=0\) then last term is \(P^{c4}c5\) (can be \(P^3\)), but then you still have \(P c2 t^{c3}\) as the only t-term (good). So choose \(c4=3\), \(c6=0\), and \(c3=-4.532...\). Then polynomial part is \(P^3 c5 + P^2 c0 + P c1\). But GT polynomial has also a linear term (yes) and quadratic and cubic (yes). Works. Potentially matchable.

13-14. Include \(P*c3*exp(P*c4)\). To remove exp(P*...) need c3=0, then polynomial part is \(P^3\) and \(P^2\) and linear plus \(P*c6*t^{c7}\). But note they also have an extra standalone \(+P\) (13) or \(+P*c8\) (14) which can be absorbed into linear coefficient (set c8 accordingly; in 13 the +P is fixed but can be absorbed by adjusting other linear coefficients). So after killing exp term, these can match (with \(c7=-4.532...\)). Potentially matchable.

15. Has \(P*c3*log(P*c4+1)\); must set c3=0. Then left \(P*c0*exp(P*c1)+P*c2+P*c5*t^{c6}+P*c7\). Need exp removed: set c1=0, then only linear terms, no \(P^2,P^3\). No match.

16. Entire expression over \((P*c1+c2)\) plus a \(t\)-term also over that denominator. Cannot equal a polynomial in P for all P unless denominator is constant (c1=0), then it becomes a polynomial up to \(P^3\) plus \(t^{c7}\) term not multiplied by P in the last numerator term \(c9*t^{c7}/c2\) (GT has no pure t-term). You could set c9=0 to remove it. Then you can match cubic/quadratic/linear and \(P*t^{-a}\) via \(P*c6*t^{c7}/c2\) with negative exponent. Potentially matchable.

17. Has \(P^{c4}c5*exp(c6*t)\). To match GT must remove exp(c6*t) by setting c6=0, then term becomes \(P^{c4}c5\) (can be cubic). Then choose \(P*c2*t^{c3}\) with negative exponent. Potentially matchable.

18-22. Contain exp(t) or log terms or extra exp(P*c7) etc; can often be zeroed, but those that remain typically lack a free cubic term unless there is a \(P^{c6}\) etc. 18 has \(P^{c6}c7*exp(c8*t)\): to remove exp(t) set c8=0, then it’s \(P^{c6}c7\) (cubic possible). With rational term \(P*c4/(P+c5)\) must set c4=0. Then it reduces to polynomial + \(P*t^{c3}\) + \(P^{c6}\). Potentially matchable.
19 has log(P*c7+1) must set c6=0; then no cubic. No match.
20 has exp(P*c6) term; must set c5=0 and exp(P*c1) to constant (c1=0) leaving only linear. No match.
21 has exp(P*c7) must set c6=0; then no cubic. No match.
22 has exp(t)*log(...) must set c5=0; then no cubic. No match.

23-24. Only linear in P plus power terms \(P^{c3}\), \(P^{c5}\) etc but no \(P*t^{-a}\) term of the form \(P/t^a\) (they have \(P*c1*t^{c2}\) which could be negative exponent, yes). However polynomial in P: you can get at most two power terms besides linear; could fit cubic and quadratic by choosing exponents 2 and 3. So potentially matchable.

25. Has rational \(P*c4/(P*c5+c6)\) and \(c8/(P*c5+c6)\). To remove rationals set c4=0 and c8=0. Then left exp(P*c1) term; set c1=0. Leaves only linear + \(P*t^{c3}\). No cubic. No match.

29. Has \(c4*exp(P*c5)\) and sine; set both coefficients to 0. Then left \(P^2 c0 + P c1 + P c2 t^{c3}\): no cubic. No match.

34-35. Have cubic/quadratic/linear plus \(P*t^{c5}\) and extra \(P^{c7}c8\) etc; can set extra power coefficient to 0 if unwanted. Can match. Potentially matchable.

36. Has exp(P*c5) and sine; set their coefficients to 0 -> no cubic. No match.

37. Has rational \(P*c6/(P+c7)\); must set c6=0. Remaining can make cubic via \(P*P^{c1}c2\) with \(c1=2\), and \(P*c4*t^{c5}\) with negative exponent. Potentially matchable.

38. Has \(P*c1*exp(P*c2)\) must set c1=0; then no cubic. No match.

39-43. These are polynomial-in-P plus \(P*t^{c4}\) and possibly extra power terms; many can be tuned to cubic/quadratic/linear and set extra terms to 0. Potentially matchable when a cubic term exists (via \(P^{c7}\) etc). If no cubic term present, no match.

44-45. Include \(P*c4*exp(P*c5)\) (kill by c4=0) and have power terms \(P^{c6}\) etc; can create cubic and quadratic and linear, and \(P*t^{c2}\) can be negative exponent. Potentially matchable.

47. Has cubic/quadratic/linear and \(P*t^{c7}\). Potentially matchable.

48. Has rational in P; to remove, set those coefficients to 0, leaving \(P*c0 + P*c1*t^{c2} + P^{c6}c7\). Only one power term besides linear, can’t generally match both \(P^2\) and \(P^3\). No match.

49. Has sine; set c6=0. Then only \(P^2\) and linear and \(P*t^{c4}\), no cubic. No match.

50-52. Exponential-in-P terms; to remove need coefficients 0, then typically no cubic. No match.

53-56,60-61,65-66. Trig/extra additive constants; can be zeroed, but remaining forms generally lack a cubic term (they’re \(P^2 + P + P*t^{c3}\) plus maybe constants). No match.

57-59,62-63,67. exp(P*c1) terms: to make polynomial must set c1=0, leaving only linear + \(P*t^{c3}\) plus maybe rational/log; cannot get cubic. No match.

64,69. Log/rational forms; even if logs removed, no cubic generally. No match.

Key point: At least one candidate must be able to exactly reproduce:
- a cubic polynomial in \(P\) with no constant term, and
- a term \(kP t^{-a}\).

Candidates 3,4,5,8,9,12,13,14,16,17,18,23,24,26,27,28,31,34,35,37,39-43,44-47 can all be parameterized to that exact functional class (cubic-in-P + \(P t^{\text{const}}\) with negative exponent), by zeroing extraneous terms and choosing exponents appropriately. Therefore at least one match exists.

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare each candidate to it.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(t,P) = 0.1404 \cdot (-1 + P/4.532) \cdot (1 - P/78.49) \cdot P + 0.1404 \cdot P / t^{4.532}$$

Let me expand the first part:
$$(-1 + P/4.532)(1 - P/78.49) = -1 + P/78.49 + P/4.532 - P^2/(4.532 \cdot 78.49)$$

So the GT becomes:
$$0.1404 \cdot P \cdot \left(-1 + P/78.49 + P/4.532 - P^2/(4.532 \cdot 78.49)\right) + 0.1404 \cdot P \cdot t^{-4.532}$$

$$= 0.1404 \cdot \left(-P + P^2/78.49 + P^2/4.532 - P^3/(355.7) \right) + 0.1404 \cdot P \cdot t^{-4.532}$$

The GT has the form:
$$\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \gamma P + \delta P \cdot t^{-4.532}$$

where $\alpha, \beta, \gamma, \delta$ are specific constants. This is a **cubic polynomial in P** plus a **P·t^c** term.

Specifically:
- $P^3$ term: $-0.1404/(4.532 \times 78.49)$
- $P^2$ term: $0.1404 \cdot (1/78.49 + 1/4.532)$
- $P$ term: $-0.1404$
- $P \cdot t^{-4.532}$ term: $0.1404$

So the GT = $a_3 P^3 + a_2 P^2 + a_1 P + a_4 P t^{c}$ where $c = -4.532$.

The basis functions are: $P^3$, $P^2$, $P$, $P \cdot t^c$.

Now I'll check each candidate to see if it can be reduced to this form.

### Candidate 1: $P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + P c_2 t^{c_3} + P c_4/(P+c_5) + c_6 \sin(Pc_7+c_8)$
Has $\sin$ term and $P/(P+c_5)$ rational term. The $\sin$ can be zeroed ($c_6=0$). The rational term $Pc_4/(P+c_5)$ cannot produce $P^3$. Missing $P^3$ term. 

Wait - let me reconsider. $Pc_4/(P+c_5)$ is a rational function, not a polynomial. The GT is purely polynomial in P (plus the t term). So this candidate has a rational function that can't be eliminated (unless $c_4=0$, but then we lose degrees of freedom). With $c_6=0$ and $c_4=0$: $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + Pc_2 t^{c_3}$ — missing $P^3$.

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 2: Complex rational expression with $\exp(Pc_1)$
Setting $c_1=0$: $\exp(0)=1$, so:
$$\frac{P^2 c_0 + Pc_4 + Pc_5 t^{c_6} + Pc_7 + c_8 t^{c_6}}{Pc_2+c_3}$$

This is a rational function in P. For it to equal $a_3P^3 + a_2P^2 + a_1P + a_4Pt^c$, we need:
$$(a_3P^3 + a_2P^2 + a_1P + a_4Pt^c)(Pc_2+c_3) = P^2c_0 + P(c_4+c_7) + Pc_5t^{c_6} + c_8t^{c_6}$$

The left side has $P^4$ terms, but the right side doesn't. So $a_3 c_2 = 0$. If $c_2=0$: LHS = $c_3(a_3P^3+...)$, RHS has max $P^2$. Doesn't work. If $a_3=0$: GT requires $a_3 \neq 0$.

Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 3: $P^2 c_0 + P \cdot P^{c_1} \cdot c_2 + Pc_3 + Pc_4(c_5+t)^{c_6} + Pc_7$

$P \cdot P^{c_1} = P^{1+c_1}$. Set $c_1=2$ to get $P^3$: $c_2 P^3 + c_0 P^2 + (c_3+c_7)P + c_4 P(c_5+t)^{c_6}$.

For the t-term: $P(c_5+t)^{c_6}$. GT needs $P \cdot t^{-4.532}$. $(c_5+t)^{c_6} \neq t^{c_6}$ unless $c_5=0$. If $c_5=0$: $Pc_4 \cdot t^{c_6}$. Then we get $c_2P^3 + c_0P^2 + (c_3+c_7)P + c_4Pt^{c_6}$. This matches the GT form! Set $c_6=-4.532$.

Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 4: $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + Pc_2(Pc_3)^{c_4} + Pc_5(c_6+t)^{c_7} + Pc_8$

$P \cdot c_2 \cdot (Pc_3)^{c_4} = c_2 c_3^{c_4} P^{1+c_4}$. Set $c_4=2$: $c_2 c_3^2 P^3$. Set $c_6=0$: $c_5 t^{c_7} P$. Then: $c_2c_3^2 P^3 + c_0 P^2 + (c_1+c_8)P + c_5 P t^{c_7}$. Matches GT form.

Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 5: $P^3 c_0 + P^2(c_1+c_2+c_3) + P(c_4+c_5) + Pc_6(c_7+t)^{c_8}$

Set $c_7=0$: $Pc_6 t^{c_8}$. Then: $c_0 P^3 + (c_1+c_2+c_3)P^2 + (c_4+c_5)P + c_6 P t^{c_8}$. Matches GT form.

### Candidate 6: $Pc_0 \exp(Pc_1) + Pc_2 t^{c_3} + Pc_4 + P^{c_5}c_6$

Set $c_1=0$: $Pc_0 + Pc_2 t^{c_3} + Pc_4 + c_6 P^{c_5}$. This gives $(c_0+c_4)P + c_2 P t^{c_3} + c_6 P^{c_5}$. Only one power of P from $P^{c_5}$. Need both $P^2$ and $P^3$. Can't match.
